<Gmap_id>0x80d95504374d882b:0xc383dd99076c8eb8<//Gmap_id>< review>
I have been here twice. I love that they use organic friendly products. They are located in an office park and are very unassuming. It's a cute place with a good selection of services. They have a small relaxation area and no showers or locker room area so it doesnt really feel like a spa.  The massage and facial I had were both good. They have dry saunas (hence why it would be great to have a shower)  and other wellness services. They have memberships as well. The prices seem just a little high considering they are missing some of the day spa amenities. Still a good place to try if you like more natural products.
Tip: they provide robes but not slippers so if you are doing a spa package, bring your own sandals!</review>

< Review>
I purchased a set of tires for my Prius on Dec. 6.  Bud's had done well for me on previous occasions, but not this time.   The staff was still friendly, but service was lacking.
First, I was told that there was a $50 mail-in rebate on the tires I purchased.  When I got home and looked for the rebate, it had expired 5 months before.
Second, I noticed that my average gas mileage had dropped by 10% for 3 tanks of gas.  I thought it may have been the tires.  But on a routine maintenance check, the tire air pressure was about 22 psi. The door frame placard clearly says 32 psi. This is something the staff should have known about and done correctly.
I'm now questioning whether I'll be back or not.
I was going to e-mail them directly and give them a chance to address this, but there's no e-mail listed on their website.</Review>

< Review>
I am addicted to the French Corner!  Not only is the food so yummy and unique, it has also become my favorite place to stop for an amazing latte and read one of my books. It's charming with its jazzy French music playing all the time. Everyone in the cafe is so friendly and personal too. Your treated like your special when you are there. The owner is especially fun to talk to. She is very passionate about her life in Paris and is exceptionally passionate about fresh organic ingredients in her menu and recipes. Her attention to detail shows. I wish I could recommend one special dish but because I love everything so much, go ahead and just pick one...you won't be sorry. I've noticed now that I'm a regular that she has lots of other fans like myself. I'm starting to feel like I'm really in a Paris Cafe!
BTW - It's very dog-friendly so bring your pup to join you!</Review>

I ordered the four cheese melted yummy baguette sandwich and delicious organic walnut cranberry salad!  Hearty and healthy!  We arrived with plenty of tables from which to choose.  Be prepared to park and walk.  It's worth to park a block or two away since street space is competitive.

Enjoy your meal and scrumptious dessert!  They have gluten free pies so your taste buds will be grateful if you are gluten in tolerate!  God bless and have a great time at this truly sweet gem on Highway 101!</review>

< Review>
Went for lunch with a friend on June 28th, the line was out the door when we first got there. It's really awkward, because people are coming out of the doorway after they order and the people waiting to order are also using the same tight doorway. Not a good impression. Excuse me, oh, excuse me, oh pardon me. Not a good start.
The young man taking the orders was obviously really really new, no greeting, no personality, no voice, maybe he was scared? Strange to say the least.
We ate in the back, there is a nice patio that is hidden, west of where you order. Nice and quiet and perfect for conversation.
I ordered the daily special, think it was chicken salad in a sandwich, my friend ordered a ham sandwich. They were good. I think we missed out on the real specialities - we saw the most delicious coffee's getting served and bakery items that make your mouth water.  I will go back, give them another chance and try the bakery items.
3 stars for service and awkward ordering process</Review>

<rate>4<//rate><Date>1591129125306< /Date>< Review>
LOOKS CUTE ! My wife and I spotted this new cafe for the first time last Sunday so we decided to try it out. We locked up our bikes and made our way inside the cafe to place an order. It's got to be the smallest cafe we've ever been in without a doubt. All the tables and chairs are on a narrow terrace outside of the cafe which is on the ground floor of a recently built row home fronting the 101. We ordered a Cappuccino, an Iced Latte and a Caprese Sandwich on a Baguette. For such a tiny place there was quite a large amount of quality looking pastries and quiches on display...even a rest room just inside the entrance. We found a table and a couple of chairs down the back of the narrow terrace and soon after our lunch order arrived. My wife's Cappuccino was quite good as was my Iced Latte. We shared the Caprese Sandwich and it was fine. Overall we thought our food and drinks were reasonable value, the service was fast enough and friendly but the location is cramped to say the least and horribly noisy. It's a strange claustrophobic space for a cafe even though the owner obviously knows her stuff.<//Review>

<date>1602452645348</date><Rate>5</Rate>< review>
Really busy place on a Sunday afternoon. They have excellent social distancing practices. We had sandwiches - chicken salad and tuna - on incredibly tasty bread with excellent texture and remarkable crust. They have extensive wine selections; not a big surprise given the location.  Some good deals on local labels. The cheese section features both local and area cheeses.  Of note, they sell Toma cheese. Maybe not a big deal locally but a hard found delicacy where I live in the Midwest. The place is crammed with delicacies and stuff; too much to look at or sample in one visit. Give yourself time for more than one visit.< /review>

< Text>
I had visited here before the new owners, and wasn't impressed.. now it's my favorite place to eat, drink and shop in Napa Valley. A complete turnaround as far as what they serve and sell. When we stopped for lunch in July they had a charred corn pizza on the menu that sounded so strange we had to try it. Now we can't stop thinking about it and craving it! Stopped in again this week and we thought it was perfect last time, but they have continued to offer even better experiences. Don't overlook the wine tastings in the back - they are some of the best in Napa Valley. Enjoy the opportunity to taste small volume offerings that you can't find anywhere else by the splash, half or full glass serving.

An excellent cheese selection, and the salads and sandwiches that you can enjoy there or take with are delicious! If you are touring Napa Valley, make this your go to destination.</Text>

<Text>While I live in Napa Valley sometimes forget about going to the touristy spots.  Our firms Summer Interns were coming to our St. Helena office for lunch.  Decided to have OVG cater it.  The entire staff was so helpful and Barry, handled all the various dietary requests like a champ. Our firm Partners and Interns loved their various salads and sandwiches. <rating>1< /rating><Text>I am a local living in Napa and have been going to Oakville Grocery for 7 years.  I also own a wine tour company and have personally brought 400-500 guests there for lunch over the last 4 years.  I am sad to say that the complaints/disappointments by my guests and myself have started to exceed the positive experiences.  The icing on the cake was 2 days ago when I called in an order (knowing it was a busy Saturday) for 4 sandwiches and was quoted 30 minutes for them to be ready.  When I came in 1 hour later to pick up the sandwiches, none of them were made; there was one employee actively making sandwiches, 2 employees just talking and one employee working the cash register and a large crowd of guests standing around waiting to pay and get their sandwiches.  This would be similar to Silver Oak, for example, having one employee pouring wine for all of their guests on one of the busiest Saturdays of the year.  Oakville Grocery set a new record of 1 hour and 15 minutes to complete the order for 4 sandwiches.  This is just one of many, many similar experiences which I will not list for times sake.  They have a staff turnover like a revolving door (I see new faces every month and always seem to be "understaffed" when I inquire as to why everything takes so long.  It's unfortunate that a historical property that has been in business since 1881 and knows very well how busy season works from year to year is so poorly managed and provides such poor service.  They even had a chance to make everything flow smoother in 2012 when they remodeled and still did not get it right.<//Text><pictures>None<//pictures><Resp>None</Resp><gmapID>0x8084544b41c336fd:0x47087a7305951bc9</gmapID></record></dataset><record>

<Text>When it costs $25 for 2 "nitro" coffees and 2 mediocre cookies, there is something wrong.  I'm a Napa native and okay with the fact that things costs more in Napa. But unlike many other places our high prices usually reflect high quality.  I actually am not a big fan of Nitro coffee but since Oakville Grocery doesn't offer iced coffee I went ahead and ordered it.  Usually nitro coffee is creamy with a little bit of a head on it, similar to a beer. My very expensive nitro was really just iced coffee from a beer keg.  In addition I had some friends order $13 sandwiches.  They didn't like the price, but they disliked the service even more.
